5430<section id="_575">

5431<h4 id="_575_toc">

5432North American cooperative and consortium trial results</h4>

5433<p id="_1876" tabindex="-1">

5434A series of North American trials have evaluated response-based and risk-adapted therapy.</p>

5435<p id="_1877" tabindex="-1">

5436Evidence (response-based and risk-adapted therapy):</p>

5437<div class="pdq-content-list">

5438<ol id="_1878">

5439<li>

5440The Pediatric Oncology Group organized two trials featuring response-based, risk-adapted therapy with ABVE [<a href="#cit/section_6.62">

544162</a>

5442] for favorable low-stage patients and dose-dense ABVE-PC for unfavorable advanced-stage patients in combination with 21 Gy IFRT.[<a href="#cit/section_6.19">

544319</a>

5444]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5445<ul id="_1879">

5446<li>

5447Children and adolescents with low-risk Hodgkin lymphoma (stages I, IIA, IIIA1) treated with IFRT (25.5 Gy) after achieving CR to two cycles of DBVE (doxorubicin, bleomycin, vincristine, and etoposide) had outcomes comparable to those not in CR after two cycles of DBVE who were then treated with a total of four cycles of DBVE and IFRT (25.5 Gy). This response-dependent approach permitted reduction in chemotherapy exposure in 45% of patients.[<a href="#cit/section_6.62">

544862</a>

5449]</li>

5450<li>

5451A dose-dense, early response&#8211;based treatment approach with ABVE-PC permitted reduction in chemotherapy exposure in 63% of patients who achieved a rapid early response after three ABVE-PC cycles.[<a href="#cit/section_6.19">

545219</a>

5453][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5454Level of evidence B1</a>

5455] </li>

5456<li>

5457The 5-year EFS rate was comparable for rapid early responders (86%) and slow early responders (83%) treated with three and five cycles of ABVE-PC, respectively, followed by 21 Gy radiation. Patients who received dexrazoxane had more hematological and pulmonary toxicity.[<a href="#cit/section_6.19">

545819</a>

5459]</li>

5460<li>

5461Although etoposide is associated with an increased risk of therapy-related acute myeloid leukemia with 11q23 abnormalities, the risk is very low in those treated with ABVE or ABVE-PC without dexrazoxane.[<a href="#cit/section_6.16">

546216</a>

5463,<a href="#cit/section_6.66">

546466</a>

5465]</li>

5466</ul>

5467</div>

5468</li>

5469<li>

5470A large COG study (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00004010">

5471COG-59704</a>

5472) evaluated response-adapted therapy featuring four cycles of the dose-intensive BEACOPP regimen (bleomycin, etoposide, doxorubicin, cyclophosphamide, vincristine, procarbazine, prednisone), followed by a sex-tailored consolidation for pediatric patients with stages IIB, IIIB with bulky disease, and IV Hodgkin lymphoma.[<a href="#cit/section_6.64">

547364</a>

5474][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5475Level of evidence B4</a>

5476] For girls with a rapid early response, an additional four courses of COPP/ABV (without IFRT) were given. Boys with a rapid early response received two cycles of ABVD followed by IFRT. Slow early responders received four additional courses of BEACOPP and IFRT. Eliminating IFRT from the girls' therapy was intended to reduce the risk of breast cancer. Key findings include the following:[<a href="#cit/section_6.64">

547764</a>

5478]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5479<ul id="_1880">

5480<li>

5481Rapid early response (defined by resolution of B symptoms and &gt;70% reduction in tumor volume) was achieved by 74% of patients after four cycles of BEACOPP.</li>

5482<li>

5483The 5-year EFS rate was 94%, with a median follow-up time of 6.3 years.</li>

5484<li>

5485Early intensification followed by less-intense response-based therapy results in high EFS.</li>

5486</ul>

5487</div>

5488<p id="_1881" tabindex="-1">

5489However, infectious complications during therapy and the long-term risks of infertility and subsequent neoplasms undermine this approach as an optimal treatment, particularly in light of newer and safer strategies.</p>

5490</li>

5491<li>

5492The Stanford, St. Jude Children's Research Hospital, and Boston Consortium administered a series of risk-adapted trials over the last 20 years. Key findings include the following:<div class="pdq-content-list">

5493<ul id="_1882">

5494<li>

5495Nonalkylating-agent chemotherapy (e.g., methotrexate or etoposide) instead of alkylating-agent chemotherapy results in an inferior EFS among patients with unfavorable clinical presentations.[<a href="#cit/section_6.67">

549667</a>

5497,<a href="#cit/section_6.68">

549868</a>

5499]</li>

5500<li>

5501The combination of vinblastine, doxorubicin, methotrexate, and prednisone (VAMP) is an effective regimen (10-year EFS rate, 89%) for children and adolescents with favorable-risk disease (low-stage nodular lymphocyte-predominant and classical Hodgkin lymphoma without B symptoms or bulky disease) when used in combination with response-based LD-IFRT (15&#8211;25.5 Gy).[<a href="#cit/section_6.60">

550260</a>

5503]</li>

5504<li>

5505Patients with favorable-risk Hodgkin lymphoma treated with four cycles of VAMP chemotherapy alone who achieved an early CR had a comparable 5-year EFS rate to those treated with four cycles of VAMP chemotherapy plus 25.5 Gy IFRT (89% vs. 88%).[<a href="#cit/section_6.69">

550669</a>

5507]</li>

5508</ul>

5509</div>

5510</li>

5511<li>

5512The COG <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00025259">

5513AHOD0031 (NCT00025259)</a>

5514 study enrolled 1,712 patients in a randomized controlled trial to evaluate the role of early

5515chemotherapy response in tailoring subsequent therapy in pediatric intermediate-risk Hodgkin lymphoma. Intermediate-risk Hodgkin lymphoma was defined as Ann Arbor stages IB, IAE, IIB, IIAE, IIIA, IVA with or without bulky disease, and IA or IIA with bulky disease. All patients received two cycles of ABVE-PC followed by response evaluation.[<a href="#cit/section_6.18">

551618</a>

5517]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5518<ol id="_1883" class="lower-alpha">

5519<li>

5520 Rapid early responders (defined by CT imaging after two cycles) received two additional ABVE-PC cycles, followed by CR evaluation. <div class="pdq-content-list">

5521<ul id="_816">

5522<li>

5523Rapid early responders with CR at the end of chemotherapy (based on CT imaging and negative PET or gallium scans) were randomly assigned to receive either IFRT or no additional therapy.</li>

5524<li>

5525Rapid early responders with less than a CR were nonrandomly assigned to IFRT. </li>

5526</ul>

5527</div>

5528</li>

5529<li>

5530Slow early responders were randomly assigned to receive two additional ABVE-PC cycles with or without two cycles of dexamethasone, etoposide, cisplatin, and cytarabine (DECA). All slow early responders were assigned to receive IFRT.</li>

5531</ol>

5532</div>

5533<p id="_1884" tabindex="-1">

5534Key 4-year OS and EFS outcomes from this trial include the following:</p>

5535<div class="pdq-content-list">

5536<ul id="_1885">

5537<li>

5538Early response was an important prognostic factor. Overall EFS rate was 85.0% and significantly (<em>

5539P</em>

5540 &lt; .001) higher for rapid early responders (86.9%) than for slow early responders (77.4%).</li>

5541<li>

5542 The OS rate was 97.8% and significantly (<em>

5543P</em>

5544 &lt; .001) higher for rapid early responders (98.5%) than for slow early responders (95.3%).</li>

5545<li>

5546Approximately 45% of patients were rapid early responders and achieved CR by the end of chemotherapy. For this population, the EFS rate did not differ significantly (<em>

5547P</em>

5548 = .11) among those who were randomly assigned to IFRT (87.9%) versus no IFRT (84.3%). The OS rate was 98.8% (95% confidence interval [CI], 96.8%&#8211;99.5%) for those receiving IFRT and 98.8% (95% CI, 96.9%&#8211;99.6%) for those receiving chemotherapy alone.</li>

5549<li>

5550Despite achieving rapid early response or CR, stage I or stage II patients with bulky mediastinal adenopathy and anemia had significantly better EFS when randomly assigned to IFRT after four cycles of ABVE-PC.[<a href="#cit/section_6.52">

555152</a>

5552]</li>

5553<li>

5554Approximately 20% of patients were slow early responders. For this population, the EFS rate did not differ significantly (<em>

5555P</em>

5556 = .11) among those who were randomly assigned to DECA (79.3%) versus no DECA (75.2%).</li>

5557<li>

5558Study results confirm the prognostic significance of early chemotherapy response and support the safety of avoidance of IFRT based on rapid early response with CR by the end of chemotherapy.</li>

5559</ul>

5560</div>

5561<p id="_1945" tabindex="-1">

5562An analysis of patterns of failure among patients who relapsed while enrolled in the <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00025259">

5563AHOD0031 (NCT00025259)</a>

5564 study demonstrated that first relapses occurred more often within the previously irradiated field and within initially involved sites of disease, including both bulky and nonbulky sites.[<a href="#cit/section_6.49">

556549</a>

5566]</p>

5567</li>

5568<li>

5569The COG <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00302003">

5570AHOD0431 (NCT00302003)</a>

5571 study used a response-directed treatment strategy for children and adolescents with stage I and stage IIA, nonbulky disease. Chemotherapy sensitivity was assessed by 18F-FDG PET response after one and three cycles of doxorubicin, vincristine, prednisone, and cyclophosphamide (AV-PC) chemotherapy. LD-IFRT (21 Gy) was administered only to patients who did not achieve a complete remission after chemotherapy. The protocol also incorporated a standardized salvage regimen (vinorelbine and ifosfamide plus dexamethasone, etoposide, cisplatin, and cytarabine) for low-risk recurrences (defined as stage I/II, nonbulky disease, regardless of time to relapse) after treatment with chemotherapy alone.[<a href="#cit/section_6.41">

557241</a>

5573]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5574<ul id="_1886">

5575<li>

5576At 4 years, the OS rate was 99.6%, with 49.0% in remission after treatment with minimal chemotherapy alone and 88.8% in remission without receiving high-dose chemotherapy with stem cell rescue or more than 21 Gy IFRT.[<a href="#cit/section_6.41">

557741</a>

5578]</li>

5579<li>

5580Factors predicting favorable EFS after a limited chemotherapy response-based approach included mixed-cellularity histology, low erythrocyte sedimentation rate, and negative 18F-FDG PET after one cycle.[<a href="#cit/section_6.41">

558141</a>

5582]</li>

5583<li>

5584Extended follow-up of this trial confirmed a significantly higher rate of relapse among patients with a slow early response by PET after one cycle, which was mitigated by adding 21 Gy of IFRT.[<a href="#cit/section_6.70">

558570</a>

5586][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5587Level of evidence B4</a>

5588]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5589<ul id="_2061">

5590<li>

5591For patients with a rapid early response, the 10-year PFS rate was 96.6% with IFRT and 84.1% without IFRT (<em>

5592P</em>

5593 = .10).</li>

5594<li>

5595For patients with a slow early response, the 10-year PFS rate was 80.9% with IFRT and 64% without IFRT (<em>

5596P</em>

5597 =.03).</li>

5598<li>

5599Among the 90 patients with a rapid early response who did not receive IFRT, all 14 relapses included an initial disease site.</li>

5600<li>

5601Among the 45 patients with a slow early response who did not receive IFRT, 14 of the 16 relapses occurred in the initial disease site.</li>

5602<li>

5603This 3-year study was amended during the second year. All patients with equivocal or positive PET findings after one cycle were treated with IFRT even if they achieved a CR after three cycles.</li>

5604</ul>

5605</div>

5606</li>

5607</ul>

5608</div>

5609</li>

5610<li>

5611An open-label, single-arm, multicenter trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01920932">

5612NCT01920932</a>

5613) evaluated two cycles of AEPA (brentuximab vedotin substituted for vincristine in the OEPA regimen) and four cycles of CAPDAC (brentuximab vedotin substituted for vincristine in the COPDAC regimen) in 77 patients aged 18 years or younger with stage IIB, IIIB, or IV classical Hodgkin lymphoma. Residual node radiation therapy (25.5 Gy) was given at the end of all chemotherapy and only to nodal sites that did not achieve a CR at the early-response assessment after two cycles of therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_6.58">

561458</a>

5615][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5616Level of evidence B4</a>

5617]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5618<ul id="_2005">

5619<li>

5620The 3-year EFS rate (median follow-up, 3.4 years) was 97.4%, and the OS rate was 98.7%.</li>

5621<li>

5622The AEPA and CAPDAC regimens were well tolerated and allowed for omission of radiation therapy in 35% of the treated patients.</li>

5623<li>

5624 Only 4% of patients experienced grade 3 neuropathy.</li>

5625<li>

5626Compared with historical controls, residual node radiation volumes in patients requiring radiation were very small, sparing healthy surrounding tissue.</li>

5627</ul>

5628</div>

5629</li>

5630<li>

5631In the COG <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02166463">

5632AHOD1331 (NCT02166463)</a>

5633 phase III study, 587 eligible high-risk patients were randomly assigned to receive ABVE-PC or Bv-AVE-PC, a regimen that incorporates brentuximab vedotin, omits bleomycin, and reduces vincristine to one dose per treatment course (see <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/child-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_578">

5634Table 6</a>

5635). Patients aged 2 to 21 years with stage IIB with bulk, stage IIIB, and stage IV Hodgkin lymphoma were eligible.[<a href="#cit/section_6.63">

563663</a>

5637]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5638<ul id="_2060">

5639<li>

5640After a median follow-up period of 42.1 months, the 3-year EFS rate was 92.1% (95% CI, 88.4%&#8211;94.7%) for patients who received Bv-AVE-PC when compared with 82.5% (95% CI, 77.4%&#8211;86.5%; <em>

5641P</em>

5642 = .0002) for patients who received ABVE-PC.</li>

5643<li>

5644The cumulative incidence of relapse was significantly lower for patients who received Bv-AVE-PC (7.5%; 95% CI, 4.9%&#8211;10.9%) than for patients who received ABVE-PC (17.1%; 95% CI, 12.9%&#8211;21.8%).</li>

5645<li>

5646Radiation therapy was administered to patients with slow-responding lesions confirmed by PET2 imaging (defined as a five-point scale score &gt;3) and to patients with any large mediastinal masses. The percentage of patients who received radiation therapy was similar between the two arms of the study (52.7% for Bv-AVE-PC and 55.7% for ABVE-PC).</li>

5647<li>

5648Rates of febrile neutropenia, infection complications, and neuropathy were similar between the two arms of the study.</li>

5649</ul>

5650</div>

5651</li>

5652<li>

5653The <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT03907488">

5654S1826 (NCT03907488)</a>

5655 phase III study included both adolescents (aged &#8805;12 years) and adults. The study evaluated the AVD regimen (doxorubicin [Adriamycin], vinblastine, and dacarbazine) with either brentuximab vedotin (Bv) or nivolumab (N) (see <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/child-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_578">

5656Table 6</a>

5657). There were 976 eligible patients with newly diagnosed stage III or stage IV Hodgkin lymphoma who were randomly assigned to receive either Bv-AVD or N-AVD. Granulocyte colony-stimulating factor was required for patients who received Bv-AVD and optional for patients who received N-AVD. The cardioprotectant, dexrazoxane, was allowed for all patients, per the investigator's choice. Radiation therapy for pediatric patients was based on the end-of-treatment imaging evaluation after completion of six cycles of systemic therapy. The use of the AVD backbone with either agent was to reduce or avoid radiation therapy and reduce the use of alkylating agents.[<a href="#cit/section_6.59">

565859</a>

5659]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5660<ul id="_2086">

5661<li>

5662Patients aged 12 to 17 years accounted for approximately 25% of the study's total accrual.</li>

5663<li>

5664Patients with stage IV Hodgkin lymphoma represented 62% to 65% of enrollees, and B symptoms were present in 56% to 58% of patients.</li>

5665<li>

5666Results for this study were released early at a planned interim analysis because the primary PFS endpoint crossed the protocol-specified monitoring boundary. </li>

5667<li>

5668The 1-year PFS rate favored N-AVD over Bv-AVD (94% versus 86%, respectively) after a median follow-up of 12.1 months. The hazard ratio (HR) was 0.48 (99% CI, 0.27&#8211;0.87). The HR for the cohort of patients who were aged 12 to 17 years was the same as the HR for the overall study population.</li>

5669<li>

5670Less than 1% of patients in either arm received consolidative radiation therapy.</li>

5671<li>

5672N-AVD was well-tolerated, with low rates of immune-related adverse events: hypothyroidism of any grade (7%), febrile neutropenia (5%), and grade 3 or higher peripheral neuropathy (1%).</li>

5673<li>

5674Both N-AVD and Bv-AVD were shown to be effective without radiation therapy and with less alkylator agents. However, patients who received N-AVD had a superior short-term EFS.</li>

5675<li>

5676While further follow-up is required, the authors suggested that N-AVD will likely be a new standard therapy for patients with advanced-stage Hodgkin lymphoma. </li>

5677</ul>

5678</div>

5679</li>

5680</ol>

5681</div>

5682</section>

5683<section id="_1887">

5684<h4 id="_1887_toc">

5685European multicenter trial results</h4>

5686<p id="_1888" tabindex="-1">

5687In the last 30 years, European investigators have conducted a series of risk-adapted trials evaluating sex-based treatments featuring multiagent chemotherapy with vincristine, prednisone, procarbazine, and doxorubicin (OPPA)/COPP and IFRT. </p>

5688<p id="_1889" tabindex="-1">

5689Key findings from these trials include the following:</p>

5690<div class="pdq-content-list">

5691<ol id="_1890">

5692<li>

5693Substitution of cyclophosphamide for mechlorethamine in the MOPP combination results in a low risk of subsequent myelodysplasia/leukemia.[<a href="#cit/section_6.9">

56949</a>

5695]</li>

5696<li>

5697Omission of procarbazine from the OPPA combination and substitution of methotrexate for procarbazine in the COPP combination (OPA/COMP) results in a substantially inferior EFS.[<a href="#cit/section_6.71">

569871</a>

5699]</li>

5700<li>

5701Substitution of etoposide for procarbazine in the OPPA combination (OEPA) in boys produces comparable EFS to that of girls treated with OPPA and is associated with hormonal parameters, suggesting lower risk of gonadal toxicity.[<a href="#cit/section_6.72">

570272</a>

5703]</li>

5704<li>

5705Omission of radiation for patients completely responding (defined as complete resolution or only minor residuals in all previously involved regions using clinical examination and anatomical imaging) to risk-based and sex-based OEPA or OPPA/COPP chemotherapy results in a significantly lower EFS in intermediate-risk and high-risk patients than in irradiated patients (79% vs. 91%), but no difference among nonirradiated and irradiated patients assigned to the favorable-risk group.[<a href="#cit/section_6.22">

570622</a>

5707]</li>

5708<li>

5709Substitution of dacarbazine for procarbazine (OEPA-COPDAC) in boys produces comparable results to standard OPPA-COPP in girls when used in combination with IFRT for intermediate-risk and high-risk patients.[<a href="#cit/section_6.20">

571020</a>

5711][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5712Level of evidence B4</a>

5713]</li>

5714<li>

5715A large, multinational, randomized trial (EuroNet-PHL-C1) investigated whether radiation therapy could be omitted in children (aged &lt;18 years) with intermediate- and advanced-stage classical Hodgkin lymphoma who achieved a morphological and adequate metabolic response to early chemotherapy with OEPA. The trial also studied whether modified consolidation with COPDAC (substituting dacarbazine for procarbazine in COPP) reduced gonadotoxicity.[<a href="#cit/section_6.73">

571673</a>

5717][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5718Level of evidence B1</a>

5719]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5720<ul id="_2054">

5721<li>

5722At a median follow-up of 66.5 months, the 5-year EFS rate was 90.1% (95% CI, 87.5%&#8211;92.7%) for patients who responded adequately to early chemotherapy with OEPA followed by COPP or COPDAC.</li>

5723<li>

5724In the analysis according to protocol treatment, the 5-year EFS rate was 89.9% (95% CI, 87.1%&#8211;92.8%) for individuals randomly assigned to COPP (n = 444) versus 86.1% (95% CI, 82.9%&#8211;89.4%) for those randomly assigned to COPDAC (n = 448). Similar results were observed in the intent-to-treat analysis.</li>

5725<li>

5726In a subgroup analysis (unplanned), the 5-year EFS rate among those with adequate early response to OEPA was 91.9% (95% CI, 88.1%&#8211;95.9%) with COPP and 82.9% (77.2%&#8211;89.0%) with COPDAC, but there was no difference in overall survival.</li>

5727<li>

5728A posttreatment semen analysis included 45 men at the 40-month follow-up. COPP appeared to be more gonadotoxic (19 of 23 men were azoospermic) than COPDAC (0 of 22 men were azoospermic). Biomarker analyses that included FSH and inhibin B also suggested higher prevalence of gonadotoxicity after COPP than COPDAC. Similarly, based on biomarker analyses limited to 113 women, FSH was significantly increased in 55 women who were randomly assigned to receive COPP, compared with 58 women who were randomly assigned to receive COPDAC. </li>

5729</ul>

5730</div>

5731</li>

5732<li>

5733Another EuroNet-PHL-C1 trial investigated whether radiation therapy can be omitted in patients with adequate morphological and metabolic responses to OEPA.[<a href="#cit/section_6.74">

573474</a>

5735]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5736<ul id="_2076">

5737<li>

5738Among 738 patients with early-stage disease (median follow-up period, 63.3 months), 714 patients were assigned to and received therapy in treatment group 1.</li>

5739<li>

5740Among the 713 patients in the intention-to-treat group, 440 had adequate responses to two cycles of OEPA and did not receive radiation therapy. The 5-year EFS rate was 86.5% (95% CI, 83.3%&#8211;89.8%).</li>

5741<li>

5742The 5-year EFS rate was 88.6% (95% CI, 84.8%&#8211;92.5%) for the 273 patients with adequate responses to chemotherapy who also received radiation therapy.</li>

5743<li>

5744The study findings suggested that radiation therapy can be omitted in patients with early-stage classical Hodgkin lymphoma who have had adequate responses to OEPA chemotherapy.</li>

5745</ul>

5746</div>

5747</li>

5748</ol>

5749</div>

5750</section>

5751</section>

5752<section id="_219">

5753<h3 id="_219_toc">

5754Accepted Risk-Adapted Treatment Strategies</h3>

5755<p id="_687" tabindex="-1">

5756Contemporary trials for pediatric Hodgkin lymphoma involve a risk-adapted, response-based treatment approach that titrates the length and intensity of chemotherapy and dose of radiation on the basis of disease-related factors, including stage, number of involved nodal regions, tumor bulk, the presence of B symptoms, and early response to chemotherapy as determined by functional imaging. In addition, vulnerability related to age and sex is also considered in treatment planning.</p>

5757<section id="_755">

5758<h4 id="_755_toc">

5759Classical Hodgkin lymphoma, low-risk disease</h4>

5760<p id="_882" tabindex="-1">

5761<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/child-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_589">

5762Table 7</a>

5763 summarizes the results of treatment approaches used for pediatric patients with low-risk Hodgkin lymphoma.</p>

5764<table id="_589" class="table-default expandable-container">

5765<caption>

5766Table 7. Treatment Approaches for Pediatric Patients With Low-Risk Hodgkin Lymphoma</caption>

5767<colgroup>

5768<col width="17.59%">

5769<col width="15.43%">

5770<col width="16.66%">

5771<col width="16.66%">

5772<col width="16.82%">

6455<p id="_1822" tabindex="-1">

6456 <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/child-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_759">

6457Table 10</a>

6458 summarizes the results of treatment approaches used for pediatric patients with nodular lymphocyte-predominant Hodgkin lymphoma, some of which feature surgery alone for completely resected disease and limited cycles of chemotherapy with or without LD-IFRT. Because of the relative rarity of this subtype, most trials are limited by small cohort numbers and nonrandom allocation of treatment. </p>

6686</section>

6687</section>

6688<section id="_725">

6689<h3 id="_725_toc">

6690Treatment of Adolescents and Young Adults With Hodgkin Lymphoma</h3>

6691<p id="_1824" tabindex="-1">

6692The treatment approach for adolescents and young adults with Hodgkin lymphoma may vary based on community referral patterns and age restrictions at pediatric cancer centers. The optimal approach is debatable. </p>

6693<p id="_726" tabindex="-1">

6694In patients with intermediate-risk or high-risk disease, the standard of care in adult oncology practices typically involves at least six cycles of ABVD chemotherapy that delivers a cumulative anthracycline dose of 300 mg/m<span class="sup">

66952</span>

6696.[<a href="#cit/section_6.77">

669777</a>

6698,<a href="#cit/section_6.78">

669978</a>

6700] For more information, see <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq">

6701Hodgkin Lymphoma Treatment</a>

6702. In late-health outcome studies of pediatric cancer survivors, the risk of anthracycline cardiomyopathy has been shown to exponentially increase after exposure to cumulative anthracycline doses of 250 to 300 mg/m<span class="sup">

67032</span>

6704.[<a href="#cit/section_6.79">

670579</a>

6706,<a href="#cit/section_6.80">

670780</a>

6708] Subsequent need for mediastinal radiation can further enhance the risk of a variety of late cardiac events.[<a href="#cit/section_6.81">

670981</a>

6710] In an effort to optimize disease control and preserve both cardiac and gonadal function, pediatric regimens for low-risk disease most often feature a restricted number of cycles of ABVD derivative combinations, whereas alkylating agents and etoposide are integrated into anthracycline-containing regimens for those with intermediate-risk and high-risk disease.</p>

6711<p id="_1798" tabindex="-1">

6712 No prospective studies of efficacy or toxicity in adolescent or young adults treated with pediatric versus adult regimens have been reported; however, some secondary analyses have been conducted.[<a href="#cit/section_6.82">

671382</a>

6714]</p>

6715<div class="pdq-content-list">

6716<ol id="_1892">

6717<li>

6718 A retrospective review documented the outcomes of patients aged 17 to 22 years treated in the Eastern Cooperative Oncology Group (ECOG) trials <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00003389">

6719E2496 (NCT00003389)</a>

6720 or Stanford V versus the COG trial <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00025259">

6721AHOD0031 (NCT00025259)</a>

6722.[<a href="#cit/section_6.83">

672383</a>

6724][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

6725Level of evidence C2</a>

6726]<div class="pdq-content-list">

6727<ul id="_1893">

6728<li>

6729 The 5-year failure-free survival (FFS) rates were 68% for patients in the ECOG trial and 81% for patients in the COG trial, with OS rates of 89% and 97%, respectively.</li>

6730<li>

6731Limitations of this study include differences in the study populations. More adolescents and young adults aged 17 to 22 years in the E2496 study had stage III or IV disease and B symptoms, whereas more adolescents and young adults aged 17 to 22 years in the AHOD0031 study had bulky disease and received radiation (although with smaller doses than those in E2496). Some of these differences were addressed using a propensity score analysis that confirmed inferior FFS for adolescents and young adults in the E2496 trial than those in the AHOD0031 trial. The study was also not a prospective randomized trial.</li>

6732</ul>

6733</div>

6734</li>

6735<li>

6736A comprehensive review of differences in outcomes between adolescent and young adult patients treated on pediatric versus adult trials was published.[<a href="#cit/section_6.84">

673784</a>

6738] In a retrospective analysis, adolescents (aged &#8805;15 years) who were treated on risk- and response-adapted Children&#8217;s Oncology Group Hodgkin lymphoma trials had worse EFS and OS rates than children (aged &lt;15 years). These trials included <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00302003">

6739AHOD0431 (NCT00302003)</a>

6740 for low-risk patients, <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00025259">

6741AHOD0031 [NCT00025259]</a>

6742 for intermediate-risk patients, and <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01026220">

6743AHOD0831 (NCT01026220)</a>

6744 for high-risk patients.[<a href="#cit/section_6.85">

674585</a>

6746]<div class="pdq-content-list">

6747<ul id="_2055">

6748<li>

6749After a median follow-up of 7.4 years, the unadjusted 5-year EFS rates were 80% for older patients and 86% for younger patients (HR, 1.38). </li>

6750<li>

6751The unadjusted 5-year OS rates were 96% for older patients and 99% for younger patients (HR, 2.50). In multivariable modeling, older patients were more likely to die than younger patients (HR, 3.08).</li>

6752<li>

6753Outcomes varied by histology for older patients. Older patients with non-mixed cellularity histology experienced a significantly increased risk of having an event, compared with younger patients with the same histology (HR, 1.32). Older patients with mixed cellularity had significantly worse unadjusted 5-year EFS rates (77%) than younger patients (94%) (HR, 2.93 unadjusted). This result remained significant after multivariable modeling (HR, 3.72).</li>

6754</ul>

6755</div>

6756</li>

6757</ol>

6758</div>

6759<p id="_746" tabindex="-1">

6760 The optimal approach for adolescents and young adults with Hodgkin lymphoma is complicated by critical but understudied variables. Factors such as tumor biology, disease control, supportive care needs, and long-term toxicities in adolescents and young adults with Hodgkin lymphoma require further research.</p>

6761<p id="_1894" tabindex="-1">

6762Adolescent and young adult patients with Hodgkin lymphoma should consider participating in a clinical trial. Information about ongoing clinical trials is

6763available from the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials">

6764NCI website</a>

6765.</p>

6766</section>

6767<section id="_TrialSearch_32_sid_6">

6768<h3 id="_TrialSearch_32_sid_6_toc">

6769Current Clinical Trials</h3>

6770<p id="_TrialSearch_32_22" tabindex="-1">

6771Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

6772advanced clinical trial search</a>

6773 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

6774General information</a>

6775 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

6776</section>

7129 <h2>

7130Treatment of Primary Refractory or Recurrent Hodgkin Lymphoma in Children and Adolescents</h2>

7131

7132 <div id="_section_113" class="pdq-sections">

7133<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

7134<h6>

7135In This Section</h6>

7136<ul>

7137<li>

7140</li>

7177</a>

7184</nav>

7185<p id="_688" tabindex="-1">

7186Because children and adolescents with Hodgkin lymphoma have excellent responses to frontline therapy, second-line (salvage) therapy has only been evaluated in a limited capacity. Because primary therapy fails in relatively few patients, no uniform second-line treatment strategy exists for this population.[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

71871</a>

7188]</p>

7189<p id="_1895" tabindex="-1">

7190 Adverse prognostic factors after relapse include the following:[<a href="#cit/section_7.2">

71912</a>

7192][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7193Level of evidence C1</a>

7194] </p>

7195<div class="pdq-content-list">

7196<ul id="_718">

7197<li>

7198The presence of B symptoms (fever, weight loss, and night sweats) and extranodal disease.[<a href="#cit/section_7.3">

71993</a>

7200] </li>

7201<li>

7202Early relapse (occurring 3&#8211;12 months from the end of therapy).[<a href="#cit/section_7.4">

72034</a>

7204,<a href="#cit/section_7.5">

72055</a>

7206]</li>

7207<li>

7208Inadequate response to initial second-line therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_7.5">

72095</a>

7210]</li>

7211</ul>

7212</div>

7213<p id="_719" tabindex="-1">

7214Children with localized favorable relapses (&#8805;12 months after completing therapy) whose original therapy involved reduced cycles of risk-adapted chemotherapy alone or chemotherapy with low-dose small-volume radiation therapy (consolidation therapy) have a high likelihood of achieving long-term survival after treatment with more intensive conventional chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_7.6">

72156</a>

7216,<a href="#cit/section_7.7">

72177</a>

7218]</p>

7219<p id="_1896" tabindex="-1">

7220Treatment options for children and adolescents with refractory or recurrent Hodgkin lymphoma include the following:</p>

7221<div class="pdq-content-list">

7222<ol id="_1897">

7223<li>

7224<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/child-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1898">

7225Chemotherapy and targeted therapy</a>

7226.</li>

7227<li>

7228<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/child-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1916">

7229Checkpoint inhibitor therapy</a>

7230.</li>

7231<li>

7232<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/child-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1906">

7233Chemotherapy followed by autologous hematopoietic stem cell transplant (HSCT)</a>

7234.</li>

7235<li>

7236<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/child-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1911">

7237Chemotherapy followed by allogeneic HSCT</a>

7238.</li>

7239<li>

7240<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/child-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1914">

7241Involved-site radiation therapy (ISRT)</a>

7242.</li>

7243</ol>

7245<section id="_1898">

7246<h3 id="_1898_toc">

7247Chemotherapy and Targeted Therapy</h3>

7248<p id="_1899" tabindex="-1">

7249Chemotherapy is the recommended second-line therapy. The choice of specific agents, dose intensity, and number of cycles is determined by the initial therapy, disease characteristics at progression/relapse, and response to second-line therapy.</p>

7250<p id="_1900" tabindex="-1">

7251Agents used alone or in combination regimens in the treatment of refractory or recurrent pediatric Hodgkin lymphoma include the following:</p>

7252<div class="pdq-content-list">

7253<ul id="_1901">

7254<li>

7255ICE (ifosfamide, carboplatin, and etoposide).[<a href="#cit/section_7.8">

72568</a>

7257] </li>

7258<li>

7259Ifosfamide and vinorelbine, with or without bortezomib.[<a href="#cit/section_7.9">

72609</a>

7261][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7262Level of evidence B4</a>

7263]; [<a href="#cit/section_7.10">

726410</a>

7265][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7266Level of evidence C3</a>

7267] </li>

7268<li>

7269Ifosfamide, gemcitabine, and vinorelbine.[<a href="#cit/section_7.11">

727011</a>

7271][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7272Level of evidence C1</a>

7273]</li>

7274<li>

7275Vinorelbine and gemcitabine.[<a href="#cit/section_7.12">

727612</a>

7277]; [<a href="#cit/section_7.13">

727813</a>

7279][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7280Level of evidence C2</a>

7281]</li>

7282<li>

7283Vinorelbine, gemcitabine, and dexamethasone.[<a href="#cit/section_7.14">

728414</a>

7285][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7286Level of evidence C1</a>

7287] </li>

7288<li>

7289EPIC (etoposide, prednisolone, ifosfamide, and cisplatin).[<a href="#cit/section_7.15">

729015</a>

7291]</li>

7292<li>

7293APE (cytosine

7294arabinoside, cisplatin, and etoposide).[<a href="#cit/section_7.16">

729516</a>

7296]</li>

7297<li>

7298MIED (high-dose methotrexate, ifosfamide, etoposide, and dexamethasone).[<a href="#cit/section_7.17">

729917</a>

7300]</li>

7301<li>

7302ESHAP (etoposide, methylprednisolone, high-dose cytarabine, and cisplatin).[<a href="#cit/section_7.18">

730318</a>

7304]</li>

7305<li>

7306DHAP (dexamethasone, high-dose cytarabine, and cisplatin).[<a href="#cit/section_7.19">

730719</a>

7308]</li>

7309<li>

7310Rituximab (for patients with CD20-positive disease) alone or in combination with second-line chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_7.20">

731120</a>

7312]</li>

7313<li>

7314Brentuximab vedotin has been evaluated in adults with Hodgkin lymphoma. The U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) indications for brentuximab vedotin in adult patients are as follows: (1) classical Hodgkin lymphoma after failure of autologous HSCT or after failure of at least two previous multiagent chemotherapy regimens in patients who are not autologous HSCT candidates, and (2) classical Hodgkin lymphoma at high risk of relapse or progression, as postautologous HSCT consolidation therapy. For more information, see the <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_174">

7315Treatment of Recurrent Classic HL</a>

7316 section in Hodgkin Lymphoma Treatment.<div class="pdq-content-list">

7317<ol id="_1902">

7318<li>

7319A phase I study in adults with CD30-positive lymphomas identified a recommended phase II dose of 1.8 mg/kg on an every-3-week schedule and showed an objective response rate of 50% (6 of 12 patients) at the recommended phase II dose.[<a href="#cit/section_7.21">

732021</a>

7321][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7322Level of evidence B4</a>

7323]</li>

7324<li>

7325A phase II trial in 102 adults with Hodgkin lymphoma who relapsed after autologous HSCT showed the following:[<a href="#cit/section_7.22">

732622</a>

7327-<a href="#cit/section_7.25">

732825</a>

7329]<div class="pdq-content-list">

7330<ul id="_1903">

7331<li>

7332A complete remission rate of 34% and a partial remission rate of 40% was observed.[<a href="#cit/section_7.22">

733322</a>

7334-<a href="#cit/section_7.24">

733524</a>

7336]</li>

7337<li>

7338Patients who achieved a complete remission (n = 34) had a 3-year progression-free survival (PFS) rate of 58% and a 3-year overall survival (OS) rate of 73%, with only 6 of 34 patients proceeding to allogeneic HSCT while in remission.</li>

7339<li>

7340Further follow-up demonstrated a 5-year OS rate of 41% and a PFS rate of 22%. However, patients who achieved a complete remission (38%) had a 5-year OS rate of 64% and a PFS rate of 52%.[<a href="#cit/section_7.25">

734125</a>

7342][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7343Level of evidence B4</a>

7344]</li>

7345</ul>

7346</div>

7347</li>

7348<li>

7349The number of pediatric patients treated with brentuximab vedotin is not sufficient to determine whether they respond differently than do adult patients. Clearance and volume of brentuximab vedotin significantly correlates with weight (<em>

7350P</em>

7351 &lt; .001), and its area under the curve and C max are lower in children than those reported in adult studies with weekly dosing.[<a href="#cit/section_7.26">

735226</a>

7353]</li>

7354<li>

7355The Children&#8217;s Oncology Group phase I/II study <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01780662">

7356AHOD1221 (NCT01780662)</a>

7357 investigated treatment with brentuximab vedotin and gemcitabine in 46 children and young adults with primary refractory Hodgkin lymphoma or early relapse.[<a href="#cit/section_7.27">

735827</a>

7359]<div class="pdq-content-list">

7360<ul id="_1904">

7361<li>

7362The recommended phase II dose of brentuximab vedotin was 1.8 mg/kg.</li>

7363<li>

7364Twenty-four of 42 patients (57%; 95% confidence interval [CI], 41%&#8211;72%) treated at this dose level experienced a complete response within the first four cycles. Four of 13 patients (31%) with partial response or stable disease had all target lesions with Deauville scores of 3 or less after cycle four. By modern response criteria, these are also complete responses, increasing the complete response rate to 28 of 42 patients (67%; 95% CI, 51%&#8211;80%).</li>

7365<li>

7366Compared with alternate second-line regimens, brentuximab vedotin with gemcitabine offers the advantage of avoiding agents, such as anthracyclines, alkylators, or epipodophyllotoxins, that are associated with late treatment-related sequelae.</li>

7367</ul>

7368</div>

7369</li>

7370<li>

7371Several small retrospective studies have evaluated the outcomes of pediatric and young adult patients with refractory or relapsed Hodgkin lymphoma treated with brentuximab vedotin and bendamustine. Overall results demonstrate tolerability, response, and the potential for this combination to serve as a bridge treatment to hematopoietic stem cell transplant.[<a href="#cit/section_7.28">

737228</a>

7373,<a href="#cit/section_7.29">

737429</a>

7375][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7376Level of evidence C1</a>

7377]<div class="pdq-content-list">

7378<ol id="_2062" class="lower-alpha">

7379<li>

7380One study evaluated the outcomes of 32 patients (median age, 16 years) who received up to six cycles of treatment with brentuximab vedotin (1.8 mg/kg) on day 1 and bendamustine (90&#8211;120 mg/m<span class="sup">

73812</span>

7382) on days 2 and 3.[<a href="#cit/section_7.28">

738328</a>

7384]<div class="pdq-content-list">

7385<ul id="_2063">

7386<li>

7387At the end of treatment, the overall response rate was 81%. </li>

7388<li>

7389The 3-year OS rate was 78.1%, and the 3-year PFS rate was 67%.</li>

7390</ul>

7391</div>

7392</li>

7393<li>

7394A multicenter study from four academic centers evaluated 29 patients (median age, 16 years) who received a median of three cycles of brentuximab vedotin (1.8 mg/kg) on day 1 and bendamustine (90 mg/m<span class="sup">

73952</span>

7396) on days 1 and 2 of 3-week cycles.[<a href="#cit/section_7.29">

739729</a>

7398]<div class="pdq-content-list">

7399<ul id="_2064">

7400<li>

7401Nineteen patients (66%) achieved a complete metabolic response, and 23 patients (79%) achieved an objective response. </li>

7402<li>

7403The 3-year posttreatment event-free survival rate was 65%, and the OS rate was 89%.</li>

7404</ul>

7405</div>

7406</li>

7407</ol>

7408</div>

7409</li>

7410</ol>

7411</div>

7412<p id="_1905" tabindex="-1">

7413There are ongoing trials to determine the toxicity and efficacy of combining brentuximab vedotin with chemotherapy.</p>

7414</li>

7415</ul>

7416</div>

7417</section>

7418<section id="_1916">

7419<h3 id="_1916_toc">

7420Checkpoint Inhibitor Therapy</h3>

7421<p id="_1917" tabindex="-1">

7422Treatments that block the interaction between programmed death-1 (PD-1) and its ligands have shown high levels of activity in adults with Hodgkin lymphoma.</p>

7423<p id="_1970" tabindex="-1">

7424Evidence (nivolumab):</p>

7425<div class="pdq-content-list">

7426<ol id="_1971">

7427<li>

7428The anti&#8211;PD-1 antibody nivolumab induced objective responses in 20 of 23 adult patients (87%) with relapsed Hodgkin lymphoma.[<a href="#cit/section_7.30">

742930</a>

7430]</li>

7431<li>

7432In a phase I/II study of nivolumab in children with refractory malignancies, single-agent nivolumab was tolerable and showed antitumor activity.[<a href="#cit/section_7.31">

743331</a>

7434][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7435Level of evidence C3</a>

7436]<div class="pdq-content-list">

7437<ul id="_2037">

7438<li>

7439 Among ten children with Hodgkin lymphoma, there was one complete response, two partial responses, and five cases of stable disease.</li>

7440</ul>

7441</div>

7442</li>

7443<li>

7444In a phase II study, pediatric and young adult patients (70% were younger than 18 years) with relapsed or refractory Hodgkin lymphoma were treated with nivolumab and brentuximab vedotin.[<a href="#cit/section_7.32">

744532</a>

7446]<div class="pdq-content-list">

7447<ul id="_2074">

7448<li>

7449After four induction cycles of nivolumab plus brentuximab vedotin, 59% of patients (23 of 43) achieved a complete metabolic response. </li>

7450<li>

7451Patients without a complete metabolic response also received intensification therapy with brentuximab vedotin and bendamustine before undergoing autologous HSCT. After intensification therapy and before consolidation therapy, 94% of patients achieved a complete metabolic response.</li>

7452</ul>

7453</div>

7454</li>

7455</ol>

7456</div>

7457<p id="_2042" tabindex="-1">

7458Nivolumab is FDA approved in adult patients with classical Hodgkin lymphoma who have relapsed or progressed after autologous HSCT and brentuximab vedotin or three or more lines of systemic therapy that included autologous HSCT.[<a href="#cit/section_7.30">

745930</a>

7460,<a href="#cit/section_7.33">

746133</a>

7462]</p>

7463<p id="_1947" tabindex="-1">

7464Evidence (pembrolizumab):</p>

7465<div class="pdq-content-list">

7466<ol id="_1948">

7467<li>

7468The anti&#8211;PD-1 antibody pembrolizumab produced an objective response rate of 65% in 31 heavily pretreated adult patients with Hodgkin lymphoma who relapsed after receiving brentuximab vedotin.[<a href="#cit/section_7.34">

746934</a>

7470] For more information, see the <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/adult-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_174">

7471Treatment of Recurrent Classic HL</a>

7472 section in Hodgkin Lymphoma Treatment.</li>

7473<li>

7474A phase II study of 210 adult patients (median age, 35 years; range, 18&#8211;76 years) with refractory/relapsed classical Hodgkin lymphoma who were treated with pembrolizumab reported the following:[<a href="#cit/section_7.35">

747535</a>

7476][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7477Level of evidence C3</a>

7478]<div class="pdq-content-list">

7479<ul id="_2038">

7480<li>

7481An overall response rate of 69% (95% CI, 62.3%&#8211;75.2%), with a complete response rate of 22.4% (95% CI, 6.9%&#8211;28.6%).</li>

7482</ul>

7483</div>

7484</li>

7485<li>

7486In a multicenter, nonrandomized, open-label, single-arm phase I/II study, 15 pediatric patients with relapsed or refractory Hodgkin lymphoma were treated with pembrolizumab at a dose of 2 mg/kg every 3 weeks.[<a href="#cit/section_7.36">

748736</a>

7488][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7489Level of evidence C1</a>

7490] <div class="pdq-content-list">

7491<ul id="_2039">

7492<li>

7493 Two patients achieved complete responses, and seven patients achieved partial responses, for an overall objective response rate of 60% (95% CI, 32.2%&#8211;83.7%).</li>

7494<li>

7495 Adverse events were documented in 97% of the 154 patients enrolled on the study; most were grades 1 to 2 toxicities.</li>

7496<li>

7497Grades 3 to 5 events, seen in 45% of the cases, consisted mostly of anemia and lymphopenia. </li>

7498<li>

7499Treatment interruptions were most commonly caused by transaminitis, hypertension, pleural effusion, and pneumonitis. </li>

7500<li>

7501Two deaths were attributed to drug administration (one resulting from pulmonary edema and the other from pleural effusion and pneumonitis).</li>

7502</ul>

7503</div>

7504</li>

7505</ol>

7506</div>

7507<p id="_1972" tabindex="-1">

7508<a href="https://dailymed.nlm.nih.gov/dailymed/drugInfo.cfm?setid=9333c79b-d487-4538-a9f0-71b91a02b287&amp;audience=professional" title="https://dailymed.nlm.nih.gov/dailymed/drugInfo.cfm?setid=9333c79b-d487-4538-a9f0-71b91a02b287&amp;audience=professional">

7509Pembrolizumab</a>

7510 is FDA approved for use in cases of refractory disease or relapse after three or more lines of therapy.</p>

7511<p id="_1974" tabindex="-1">

7512There are ongoing trials to determine the toxicity and efficacy of combining and/or comparing brentuximab vedotin and nivolumab with chemotherapy in pediatric patients with Hodgkin lymphoma.</p>

7513</section>

7514<section id="_1906">

7515<h3 id="_1906_toc">

7516Chemotherapy Followed by Autologous Hematopoietic Stem Cell Transplant (HSCT)</h3>

7517<p id="_1907" tabindex="-1">

7518Myeloablative chemotherapy with autologous HSCT is the recommended approach for patients who develop refractory disease during therapy or relapsed disease within 1 year after completing therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_7.8">

75198</a>

7520,<a href="#cit/section_7.37">

752137</a>

7522-<a href="#cit/section_7.39">

752339</a>

7524]; [<a href="#cit/section_7.40">

752540</a>

7526,<a href="#cit/section_7.41">

752741</a>

7528][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7529Level of evidence C1</a>

7530] This approach is also recommended for patients who have recurrent, extensive disease after the first year of completing therapy or for those with recurrent disease after initial therapy that included intensive (alkylating agents and anthracyclines) multiagent chemotherapy and radiation therapy.</p>

7531<div class="pdq-content-list">

7532<ul id="_1908">

7533<li>

7534Autologous HSCT has been preferred for patients with relapsed Hodgkin lymphoma because of the historically high transplant-related mortality (TRM) associated with allogeneic transplant.[<a href="#cit/section_7.42">

753542</a>

7536] After autologous HSCT, the projected survival rate is 45% to 70%, and the PFS rate is 30% to 89%.[<a href="#cit/section_7.24">

753724</a>

7538,<a href="#cit/section_7.40">

753940</a>

7540,<a href="#cit/section_7.43">

754143</a>

7542,<a href="#cit/section_7.44">

754344</a>

7544]; [<a href="#cit/section_7.45">

754545</a>

7546,<a href="#cit/section_7.46">

754746</a>

7548][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7549Level of evidence C1</a>

7550]</li>

7551<li>

7552Brentuximab vedotin as maintenance therapy, given for 1 year after autologous HSCT in adult patients with high risk of relapse or progression, was demonstrated to improve PFS in a randomized, placebo-controlled, phase III trial.[<a href="#cit/section_7.47">

755347</a>

7554] </li>

7555<li>

7556A multicenter, open-label, dose-escalation, phase I/II study evaluated the safety, maximum tolerated dose, and pharmacokinetics of brentuximab vedotin and identified a recommended phase II dose in 36 pediatric patients with relapsed or refractory classical Hodgkin lymphoma (n = 19) and anaplastic large cell lymphoma (n = 17). Toxicity was manageable (33% of patients had transient, limited-severity peripheral neuropathy), the maximum tolerated dose was not reached, and pediatric pharmacokinetics were similar to that of adults. The recommended phase II dose of brentuximab vedotin, 1.8 mg/m<span class="sup">

75572</span>

7558, was administered for up to 16 cycles (median, 10 cycles) on the phase II arm. Among Hodgkin lymphoma participants on the phase II arm, 47% of patients achieved an overall response (33% complete response, 13% partial response), which provided a bridge to HSCT for some patients.[<a href="#cit/section_7.48">

755948</a>

7560][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7561Level of evidence C1</a>

7562]</li>

7563<li>

7564The most commonly used preparative regimen for peripheral blood stem cell transplant is the BEAM regimen (carmustine [BCNU], etoposide, cytarabine, melphalan) or CBV regimen (cyclophosphamide, carmustine, etoposide).[<a href="#cit/section_7.38">

756538</a>

7566,<a href="#cit/section_7.43">

756743</a>

7568,<a href="#cit/section_7.44">

756944</a>

7570,<a href="#cit/section_7.46">

757146</a>

7572]; [<a href="#cit/section_7.40">

757340</a>

7574,<a href="#cit/section_7.41">

757541</a>

7576][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7577Level of evidence C1</a>

7578] Carmustine may produce significant pulmonary toxicity.[<a href="#cit/section_7.46">

757946</a>

7580]</li>

7581<li>

7582Other noncarmustine-containing preparative regimens have been used, including high-dose busulfan, etoposide, and cyclophosphamide [<a href="#cit/section_7.49">

758349</a>

7584] and lomustine, cytarabine, cyclophosphamide, and etoposide (LACE).[<a href="#cit/section_7.50">

758550</a>

7586][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7587Level of evidence C1</a>

7588]</li>

7589</ul>

7590</div>

7591<p id="_1909" tabindex="-1">

7592Adverse prognostic features for outcome after autologous HSCT include extranodal disease at relapse, bulky mediastinal mass at time of transplant, advanced stage at relapse, primary refractory disease, poor response to chemotherapy, and a positive positron emission tomography scan before autologous HSCT.[<a href="#cit/section_7.2">

75932</a>

7594,<a href="#cit/section_7.43">

759543</a>

7596,<a href="#cit/section_7.44">

759744</a>

7598,<a href="#cit/section_7.46">

759946</a>

7600,<a href="#cit/section_7.51">

760151</a>

7602,<a href="#cit/section_7.52">

760352</a>

7604]</p>

7605<p id="_1910" tabindex="-1">

7606 For more information about transplant, see <a href="/types/childhood-cancers/hp-stem-cell-transplant/autologous">

7607Pediatric Autologous Hematopoietic Stem Cell Transplantation</a>

7608 and <a href="/types/childhood-cancers/hp-stem-cell-transplant">

7609Pediatric Hematopoietic Stem Cell Transplantation and Cellular Therapy for Cancer</a>

7610. </p>

7611</section>

7612<section id="_1911">

7613<h3 id="_1911_toc">

7614Chemotherapy Followed by Allogeneic HSCT</h3>

7615<p id="_1912" tabindex="-1">

7616For patients who do not improve after autologous HSCT and

7617patients with chemoresistant disease, allogeneic HSCT has been used with encouraging results.[<a href="#cit/section_7.15">

761815</a>

7619,<a href="#cit/section_7.42">

762042</a>

7621,<a href="#cit/section_7.53">

762253</a>

7623] Investigations of reduced-intensity allogeneic transplant that typically use fludarabine or low-dose total body irradiation to provide a nontoxic immunosuppression have demonstrated acceptable rates of TRM.[<a href="#cit/section_7.54">

762454</a>

7625-<a href="#cit/section_7.57">

762657</a>

7627]</p>

7628<p id="_1913" tabindex="-1">

7629For more information about transplant, see <a href="/types/childhood-cancers/hp-stem-cell-transplant/allogeneic">

7630Pediatric Allogeneic Hematopoietic Stem Cell Transplantation</a>

7631 and <a href="/types/childhood-cancers/hp-stem-cell-transplant">

7632Pediatric Hematopoietic Stem Cell Transplantation and Cellular Therapy for Cancer</a>

7633.</p>

7634</section>

7635<section id="_1914">

7636<h3 id="_1914_toc">

7637Involved-site Radiation Therapy (ISRT)</h3>

7638<p id="_1915" tabindex="-1">

7639ISRT to sites of recurrent disease may enhance local control if these sites have not been previously irradiated. ISRT is generally administered after high-dose chemotherapy and stem cell rescue.[<a href="#cit/section_7.58">

764058</a>

7641] For patients who are not responsive to salvage therapy, ISRT may be an appropriate consideration before HSCT.[<a href="#cit/section_7.59">

764259</a>

7643,<a href="#cit/section_7.60">

764460</a>

7645] Consolidative ISRT is particularly appropriate in the following situations:[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

76461</a>

7647]</p>

7648<div class="pdq-content-list">

7649<ul id="_2029">

7650<li>

7651Low-risk patients whose positron emission tomography (PET) scans are negative after standard-dose salvage chemotherapy.</li>

7652<li>

7653Select standard-risk and/or high-risk patients who are treated with high-dose chemotherapy and HSCT.</li>

7654</ul>

7655</div>

7656</section>

7657<section id="_696">

7658<h3 id="_696_toc">

7659Response Rates for Primary Refractory Hodgkin Lymphoma</h3>

7660<p id="_697" tabindex="-1">

7661Salvage rates for patients with primary refractory Hodgkin lymphoma are poor even with autologous HSCT and radiation. However, some studies have reported that intensification of therapy followed by HSCT consolidation can achieve long-term survival.</p>

7662<p id="_1920" tabindex="-1">

7663Evidence (response to treatment of primary refractory Hodgkin lymphoma):</p>

7664<div class="pdq-content-list">

7665<ol id="_1921">

7666<li>

7667In one large series, the 5-year OS rate after primary refractory Hodgkin lymphoma was attained with aggressive second-line therapy (high-dose chemoradiation therapy) and autologous HSCT in 49% of patients.[<a href="#cit/section_7.61">

766861</a>

7669]</li>

7670<li>

7671In a Gesellschaft f&#252;r P&#228;diatrische Onkologie und H&#228;matologie (GPOH) study, patients with primary refractory Hodgkin lymphoma (progressive disease on therapy or relapse within 3 months from the end of therapy) had 10-year event-free survival (EFS) and OS rates of 41% and 51%, respectively.[<a href="#cit/section_7.4">

76724</a>

7673]</li>

7674<li>

7675A study of 53 adolescent patients like those who participated in the GPOH study had similar results for EFS and OS.[<a href="#cit/section_7.62">

767662</a>

7677] Chemosensitivity to standard-dose, second-line chemotherapy predicted better survival (OS rate, 66%), and tumors that remained refractory to chemotherapy did poorly (OS rate, 17%).[<a href="#cit/section_7.63">

767863</a>

7679]</li>

7680<li>

7681Another group reported a PFS rate of 80% post-HSCT for chemosensitive patients, compared with 0% for those with chemoresistant disease.[<a href="#cit/section_7.40">

768240</a>

7683]</li>

7684</ol>

7685</div>

7686</section>

7687<section id="_826">

7688<h3 id="_826_toc">

7689Second Relapse After Initial Treatment With Autologous HSCT</h3>

7690<p id="_827" tabindex="-1">

7691In a phase II study, patients (median age, 26.5 years) who had relapsed or refractory disease after autologous HSCT received brentuximab vedotin, with an objective response rate of 73% and a complete remission rate of 34%. Patients who achieved a complete remission (n = 34) had a 3-year PFS rate of 58% and a 3-year OS rate of 73%. Only 6 of 34 patients proceeded to allogeneic HSCT while in remission.[<a href="#cit/section_7.24">

769224</a>

7693][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

7694Level of evidence B4</a>

7695]</p>

7696</section>

7697<section id="_760">

7698<h3 id="_760_toc">

7699Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation</h3>

7700<p id="_761" tabindex="-1">

7701Information about National Cancer Institute (NCI)&#8211;supported clinical trials can be found on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search">

7702NCI website</a>

7703. For information about clinical trials sponsored by other organizations, see the <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/">

7704ClinicalTrials.gov website</a>

7705.</p>

7706<section id="_1992">

7707<h4 id="_1992_toc">

7708Anti-CD30 chimeric antigen receptor (CAR) T-cell therapy clinical trials</h4>

7709<p id="_1993" tabindex="-1">

7710Preliminary data on CAR T cells targeting CD30 have been published. In a phase I/II trial of 41 adults with multiply relapsed or refractory Hodgkin lymphoma, CD30 CAR T cells were administered after lymphoreduction with either bendamustine alone, bendamustine and fludarabine, or cyclophosphamide and fludarabine.[<a href="#cit/section_7.64">

771164</a>

7712] Treated patients had a median of seven previous lines of therapy, including brentuximab, checkpoint inhibitors, and autologous and allogeneic HSCTs. The overall response rate was 72% for the 32 patients with active disease who received fludarabine-based lymphodepletion. For all evaluable patients, the 1-year PFS rate was 36%, and the OS rate was 94%. The CD30 CAR T-cell therapy was well tolerated. </p>

7713<p id="_1994" tabindex="-1">

7714A number of clinical trials of anti-CD30 CAR T-cell therapy for patients with relapsed Hodgkin lymphoma are listed on <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/">

7715ClinicalTrials.gov</a>

7716. The following is an example of a national and/or institutional clinical trial that is currently enrolling patients younger than 18 years:</p>

7717<div class="pdq-content-list">

7718<ul id="_1995">

7719<li>

7720<strong>

7721<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02917083">

7722RELY-30 (NCT02917083)</a>

7723</strong>

7724 (CD30 CAR T Cells With or Without Cyclophosphamide and Fludarabine in Treating Participants With Relapsed or Refractory CD30-Positive Lymphoma)<strong>

7725:</strong>

7726 Patients aged 12 years and older with relapsed or refractory Hodgkin lymphoma will receive CD30 CAR T-cell therapy after chemotherapy or autologous transplant in this phase I study.</li>

7727</ul>

7728</div>

7729</section>

8023 <section id="_243">

8024

8025 <h2>

8026Late Effects From Childhood and Adolescent Hodgkin Lymphoma Therapy</h2>

8027

8028 <div id="_section_243" class="pdq-sections">

8029<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

8030<h6>

8031In This Section</h6>

8032<ul>

8033<li>

8034<a href="#_245_toc">

8035Male Gonadal Toxicity</a>

8036</li>

8037<li>

8038<a href="#_249_toc">

8039Female Gonadal Toxicity</a>

8040</li>

8041<li>

8042<a href="#_251_toc">

8043Thyroid Abnormalities</a>

8044</li>

8045<li>

8046<a href="#_300_toc">

8047Cardiac Toxicity<ul>

8048<li>

8049<a href="#_596_toc">

8050Radiation-associated cardiovascular toxicity</a>

8051</li>

8052<li>

8053<a href="#_602_toc">

8054Anthracycline-related cardiac toxicity</a>

8055</li>

8056</ul>

8057</a>

8058</li>

8059<li>

8060<a href="#_253_toc">

8061Subsequent Neoplasms</a>

8062</li>

8063</ul>

8064</nav>

8065<p id="_244" tabindex="-1">

8066Childhood and adolescent survivors of Hodgkin lymphoma may be at risk of developing numerous late complications of treatment related to radiation, specific chemotherapeutic exposures, and surgical staging.[<a href="#cit/section_8.1">

80671</a>

8068,<a href="#cit/section_8.2">

80692</a>

8070] Adverse treatment effects may impact the following:</p>

8071<div class="pdq-content-list">

8072<ul id="_1922">

8073<li>

8074Reproductive system (<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/child-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_245">

8075male gonadal toxicity</a>

8076 and <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/child-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_249">

8077female gonadal toxicity</a>

8078).</li>

8079<li>

8080Endocrine system (<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/child-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_251">

8081thyroid abnormalities</a>

8082).</li>

8083<li>

8084<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/child-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_300">

8085Cardiovascular system</a>

8086.</li>

8087<li>

8088Risk of <a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/child-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_253">

8089subsequent benign or malignant neoplasms</a>

8090.</li>

8091<li>

8092Oral/dental health.</li>

8093<li>

8094Pulmonary function.</li>

8095<li>

8096Musculoskeletal growth and development.</li>

8097<li>

8098Immune system.</li>

8099</ul>

8100</div>

8101<p id="_1923" tabindex="-1">

8102In the past 30 to 40 years, pediatric Hodgkin lymphoma therapy has changed dramatically to limit exposure to radiation and chemotherapeutic agents, such as anthracyclines, alkylating agents, and bleomycin. When counseling individual patients about the risk of specific treatment complications, the era of treatment should be considered.</p>

8103<p id="_2003" tabindex="-1">

8104In this regard, Childhood Cancer Survivor Study (CCSS) investigators determined the incidence of serious health conditions among 2,996 five-year survivors of pediatric Hodgkin lymphoma (mean age, 35.8 years), compared outcomes by treatment era and strategies, and estimated risks associated with contemporary therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_8.3">

81053</a>

8106]</p>

8107<div class="pdq-content-list">

8108<ul id="_2004">

8109<li>

8110The cumulative incidence of any grade 3 to 5 conditions by age 35 years was 31.4%. Females were twice as likely as males to experience these conditions (hazard ratio, 2.1).</li>

8111<li>

8112The decade-specific risk of grade 3 to 5 conditions declined by 20% from the 1970s to the 1990s (<em>

8113P</em>

8114 trend = .002).</li>

8115<li>

8116Compared with survivors who were treated with chest radiation therapy of 35 Gy or higher in combination with an anthracycline or alkylating agent, patients who received contemporary regimens for low- or intermediate-risk disease had an estimated 40% reduction in risk of grade 3 to 5 conditions (HR, 0.6).</li>

8117<li>

8118The risk of grade 3 to 5 conditions in survivors who had a recurrence or underwent hematopoietic stem cell transplant (HSCT) was substantially elevated and similar to that of survivors treated with high-dose, extended-field radiation therapy. </li>

8119</ul>

8120</div>

8121<p id="_716" tabindex="-1">

8122<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/child-hodgkin-treatment-pdq#_1939">

8123Table 11</a>

8124 summarizes late health effects observed in Hodgkin lymphoma survivors, followed by a limited discussion of common late effects. For a full discussion of the late effects of cancer treatment in children and adolescents, see <a href="/types/childhood-cancers/late-effects-hp-pdq">

8125Late Effects of Treatment for Childhood Cancer</a>

8126.</p>

8127<table id="_1939" class="table-default expandable-container">

8128<caption>

8129Table 11. Treatment Complications Observed in Hodgkin Lymphoma Survivors</caption>

8130<colgroup>

8131<col width="33.33%">

8132<col width="33.33%">

8133<col width="33.33%">

8134</colgroup>

8135<THead>

8136<tr>

8137<th>

8138Health Effects </th>

8139<th>

8140 Predisposing Therapy</th>

8141<th>

8142Clinical Manifestations</th>

8143</tr>

8144</THead>

8145<tbody>

8146<tr>

8147<td rowspan="2">
